<div id="review_1106115479" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1106115479" />
    <a title="Ghost Ryter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31924014-ghost-ryter"><img alt="Ghost Ryter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421367031p2/31924014.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1106115479?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ghost Ryter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ghost Ryter" href="/user/show/31924014-ghost-ryter">Ghost Ryter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31924014-ghost-ryter?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31924014-ghost-ryter?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31924014-ghost-ryter?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31924014-ghost-ryter?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31924014-ghost-ryter?shelf=he-needs-cookies">he-needs-cookies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1106115479" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14104464979088357702">Sequels tend to be disappointing. They're good books and all that, but compared to the magic and wonder and brilliance of the first book? Eh. Of the who-knows-how-many sequels I've read, there've been exactly six that I liked as much as their predecessors.<br/><br/><i>The King's Scrolls</i> is number six.<br/><br/>It has everything that I loved about Resistance. The strong message of faith, the exciting plot, the setting reminiscent of the Roman Empire, and the characters who wormed their way into my heart. (*offers Jace </span>
  <span id="freeText14104464979088357702" style="display:none">Sequels tend to be disappointing. They're good books and all that, but compared to the magic and wonder and brilliance of the first book? Eh. Of the who-knows-how-many sequels I've read, there've been exactly six that I liked as much as their predecessors.<br /><br /><i>The King's Scrolls</i> is number six.<br /><br />It has everything that I loved about Resistance. The strong message of faith, the exciting plot, the setting reminiscent of the Roman Empire, and the characters who wormed their way into my heart. (*offers Jace cookies*)<br /><br />Unlike the first book, however, <i>The King's Scrolls</i> has dragons. This or may not have had something to do with why I loved this book so much. (Dragons, as you know, make everything awesome simply by <i>existing</i>.) And don't get me started on the Cretes.... I'll just say, the next book needs to take us exploring in one of their cities.<br /><br />(Speaking of future books...Kaden needs his own book. I had thought that's what The King's Scrolls would be, but unfortunately, no. *sighs*)<br /><br />One other thing really makes this stand out from the first book, and it is that while the reader knew all throughout <i>Resistance</i> that the characters were risking execution, we see now how real that threat is. We are reminded that people's lives are at stake, and some will die--and they won't all just be red shirts. There will be characters we and our protagonists care about who are killed. (Maybe even our protagonists themselves...but let's not think about that.) The story we read is given depth, and we appreciate their faith and courage more than before.<br /><br />There were a few problems with this book. With such a large cast of characters, both new and old, I think the author had a hard time juggling them all, and some tended to vanish into the background. A couple of times Kyrin, her father, and various others did some rather stupid things that ended up causing a lot of trouble for them. Cue the frustrated character-lecturing.<br /><br />But overall, I loved this book. I'll eagerly be waiting for the next installment of The Ilyon Chronicles!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14104464979088357702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kaysie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31186796-kaysie"><img alt="Kaysie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424386016p2/31186796.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer18041799263161855014"><strong>Absolutely Wonderful!!!</strong><br/><br/>A book that catches your heart and does not let go. The characters are written with such depth that you feel as though you come to know them as you would close friends. This author has a God given talent that puts faith and the fact He is with us in the moments that are a joy and the moments that break your heart and the fact that the Lord has a plan even when we cannot see it through our tears into words that pierce the heart. He is our comfort, our joy, our peace, our He</span>
  <span id="freeText18041799263161855014" style="display:none"><strong>Absolutely Wonderful!!!</strong><br /><br />A book that catches your heart and does not let go. The characters are written with such depth that you feel as though you come to know them as you would close friends. This author has a God given talent that puts faith and the fact He is with us in the moments that are a joy and the moments that break your heart and the fact that the Lord has a plan even when we cannot see it through our tears into words that pierce the heart. He is our comfort, our joy, our peace, our Heavenly Father and Best Friend always no matter what and He is with us always holding our hearts. I love how amazingly this author captures that in words. Her books have been a blessing to me and I hope they will be a blessing to you. Looking forward to book three already </span>

<div id="review_1791367516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1791367516" />
    <a title="A.L. Buehrer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45702383-a-l-buehrer"><img alt="A.L. Buehrer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538145788p2/45702383.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1791367516?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A.L. Buehrer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="A.L. Buehrer" href="/user/show/45702383-a-l-buehrer">A.L. Buehrer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45702383-a-l-buehrer?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1791367516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10929414489126591287">After finishing Resistance, I knew I would have to continue with the Ilyon Chronicles series. I felt like there was clearly more to be explored in Ilyon, and, besides, I knew dragons were coming eventually. So here’s my quick summing up of the good, the bad and the weird, in my opinion.<br/><br/>Things I liked:<br/><br/>•	Dragons! The presence of a fantastical creature in a book will always keep my interest. Knight’s dragons were unique and had personality. I liked that some of them were “pintos.” Then there was Ge</span>
  <span id="freeText10929414489126591287" style="display:none">After finishing Resistance, I knew I would have to continue with the Ilyon Chronicles series. I felt like there was clearly more to be explored in Ilyon, and, besides, I knew dragons were coming eventually. So here’s my quick summing up of the good, the bad and the weird, in my opinion.<br /><br />Things I liked:<br /><br />•	Dragons! The presence of a fantastical creature in a book will always keep my interest. Knight’s dragons were unique and had personality. I liked that some of them were “pintos.” Then there was Gem, of course. I liked her as a character, and I hope she gets a lot of page-time in future books.<br /><br />•	The pace of this book was a lot faster than the first, and it felt like the characters were a lot less passive. There was more adventure and suspense in this plot and less time spent waiting for it to happen.<br /><br />•	Along those same lines, I appreciated the action in this book. Spying missions, fighting, dragon-flights, dragon-combat. These are good things as far as I’m concerned. Regularly seeing these characters in jeopardy made me care more about them, and their story.<br /><br />•	Once again, I’m excited by the creativity in this series’ world-building. I liked the Cretes, with their unique skills and traits and culture. I liked their fearlessness of heights, love of dragons, and long hair. I liked Captain Darq, and how that name looks written down. I wish he got a little more attention. I liked Talas too, even though I rarely go for friendly characters.<br /><br />•	There were a lot of setting changes in this book, which is also something I like. The settings felt rich and vivid, perhaps even more so than in the first book. I really liked that. I really could feel how oppressive the mining settlement was, and the freshness and freedom of the mountains.<br /><br />•	Sometimes authors give a main character siblings just so they can have siblings and really do nothing with them. Knight didn’t do this. I was really glad to see that she was investing in the character arcs of Kyrin’s older brothers. I’m glad they’re actually part of the story.<br /><br />Things I didn’t like:<br /><br />•	I was really excited for the first dragon flight scene, but in my opinion, it was kind of ruined…by Jace. Okay, confession, I’m not as crazy about Jace as I’m supposed to be. This is just a personal preference, based on opinion—not the author’s fault. If I met Jace in real life, he would probably annoy me. He’s kind of a big hunky bundle of insecurity. (I’m going to be murdered by fangirls.) I want him to toughen up and shake it off. But just as a side note, I wish I had been with Kaden on his first flight. That would have been fun. <br /><br />•	Another character I’m supposed to love, but didn’t was Timothy. Funny thing, to me, he felt like a woman. And I typically like males with some feminine qualities, but to me, Timothy’s behavior was almost indistinguishable from Kyrin’s, but a little more perfect. His fussy hand-wringing kind of got on my nerves. Once again, I’m not attacking the author about this—he’s a well-constructed character—but I just think if I knew him, I wouldn’t like him.<br /><br />•	Just one more thing. I know this is a very serious story, and it deals with a lot of grief and pain and fear. But…I wish something funny would happen now and then. <br /><br /> Things I thought were weird:<br /><br />•	Um, Leetra. I almost filed her under things I don’t like, but I feel like she has potential. But what’s wrong with her? I know, she’s a Crete, but does that really account for how stiff she is? She’s so stiff…and then, she has emotions to. Stiff emotions.<br /><br />•	Drakes. Almost filed this one under things I liked, but they fit the weird category so well. Big scary non-dragon things that came out of nowhere. Cool.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10929414489126591287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('f9ZfNi0Rdgfd1FjRX98Z8xxYAIQzjKy3AcXPohDk2KNBRKBrXSykaLOYlsDAN5yXBaAOoXiD3pdMrPNKPvDXVg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1LVFnMRRJ1EpzpwsGtmgvWuy79VGuHdV86L8wz2nts7qJ7rBtGz1PkeCUj2FMSXZckrh8A23BXW+y8ArE7O5Ow==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText18293712957451771748" style="display:none">Jaye L. Knight is an award-winning author and shameless tea addict with a passion for Christian fantasy. Armed with an active imagination and love for adventure, Jaye weaves stories of truth, faith, and courage with the message that even in the deepest darkness, God’s love shines as a light to offer hope. She writes from her home in the Northwoods of Wisconsin where she lives with her three furbaby kitties, Arthur (as in King Arthur), Timothy, and Lucy. When not writing fantasy, she can also be found dabbling in contemporary romance novels under the pen name <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18235762._Jaye_Elliot" title=" Jaye Elliot" rel="nofollow noopener"> Jaye Elliot</a>.</span>
